Table structure for table `app_settings`
--

CREATE TABLE `app_settings` (
  `setting_key` varchar(100) NOT NULL,
  `setting_value` text DEFAULT NULL
) ENGINE=InnoDB DEFAULT CHARSET=utf8mb4 COLLATE=utf8mb4_general_ci;

-- Dumping data for table `app_settings`
--

--
-- Table structure for table `auth_events`
--

CREATE TABLE `auth_events` (
  `id` int(11) NOT NULL,
  `user_email` varchar(255) NOT NULL,
  `name` varchar(255) DEFAULT NULL,
  `role` varchar(50) DEFAULT NULL,
  `event_type` varchar(50) NOT NULL,
  `timestamp` timestamp NOT NULL DEFAULT current_timestamp()
) ENGINE=InnoDB DEFAULT CHARSET=utf8mb4 COLLATE=utf8mb4_general_ci;

-- --------------------------------------------------------

--
-- Table structure for table `chats`
--

CREATE TABLE `chats` (
  `id` varchar(255) NOT NULL,
  `user_id` int(11) NOT NULL,
  `title` varchar(255) NOT NULL,
  `messages` longtext CHARACTER SET utf8mb4 COLLATE utf8mb4_bin NOT NULL CHECK (json_valid(`messages`)),
  `created_at` timestamp NOT NULL DEFAULT current_timestamp(),
  `updated_at` timestamp NOT NULL DEFAULT current_timestamp() ON UPDATE current_timestamp(),
  `timestamp` timestamp NOT NULL DEFAULT current_timestamp()
) ENGINE=InnoDB DEFAULT CHARSET=utf8mb4 COLLATE=utf8mb4_general_ci;

-- Dumping data for table `chats`

What is AI?\\nAI is defined as a branch of computer science focused on creating intelligent machines that can learn, work, and react like humans, mimicking human intelligence to perform tasks and iteratively improve based on collected information. It\'s a universal field relevant to any intellectual task, encompassing subfields from learning and perception to specific applications like chess playing, theorem proving, and disease diagnosis. The document outlines eight definitions of AI along two dimensions: concerned with thought processes vs. behavior, and measuring success by fidelity to human performance vs. an ideal performance measure (rationality).\\n\\n2. Four Approaches to AI:\\nThe text details four historical approaches to AI:\\n   Acting Humanly (Turing Test): Proposed by Alan Turing, this approach defines intelligence by a computer\'s ability to produce responses indistinguishable from a human\'s to written questions. A \\\"total Turing Test\\\" would also require computer vision and robotics for physical interaction.\\n   Thinking Humanly (Cognitive Modeling): This approach aims to understand how humans think through introspection, psychological experiments, and brain imaging, then express these theories as computer programs. Cognitive science combines AI models with psychological techniques to build testable theories of the human mind.\\n   Thinking Rationally (\\\"Laws of Thought\\\"): Rooted in Aristotle\'s logic, this approach seeks to codify \\\"right thinking\\\" using irrefutable reasoning processes (syllogisms). The logicist tradition in AI attempts to build intelligent systems based on formal logic, though challenges include formalizing informal knowledge and practical problem-solving.\\n   Acting Rationally (Rational Agent): A rational agent acts to achieve the best outcome, or the best expected outcome under uncertainty. This approach is more general than \\\"laws of thought\\\" (as correct inference is just one mechanism for rationality) and more amenable to scientific development than human-centric approaches because rationality is mathematically well-defined.\\n\\n3. The State of the Art (AI Applications):\\nAI has demonstrated significant capabilities across various applications:\\n   Robotic Vehicles: Driverless cars like STANLEY (2005 DARPA Grand Challenge winner) and CMU\\u2019s BOSS (Urban Challenge winner) navigate complex environments.\\n   Speech Recognition: Automated systems guide conversations for tasks like flight booking.\\n   Autonomous Planning & Scheduling: NASA\'s Remote Agent (first on-board autonomous planning program for spacecraft) and its successors MAPGEN and MEXAR2 for Mars missions.\\n   Game Playing: IBM\\u2019s DEEP BLUE defeated chess world champion Garry Kasparov in 1997.\\n   Spam Fighting: Learning algorithms classify billions of spam messages daily, adapting to evolving tactics.\\n   Logistics Planning: DART (Dynamic Analysis and Replanning Tool) was used during the Persian Gulf crisis to plan logistics for up to 50,000 vehicles, cargo, and personnel, drastically reducing planning time.\\n   Robotics: iRobot\'s Roomba vacuum cleaners and PackBot military robots.\\n   Machine Translation: Programs automatically translate languages (e.g., Arabic to English) using statistical models built from vast text examples.\\n\\n4. Intelligent Agents:\\nAn agent is defined as anything that perceives its environment through sensors and acts upon it through actuators (e.g., human agents use eyes\\/ears, robotic agents use cameras\\/motors, software agents use keystrokes\\/file contents). A percept is an agent\'s perceptual input at any instant, and a percept sequence is the complete history of its perceptions. An agent\'s behavior is described by an agent function (abstract mathematical description mapping percept sequences to actions) implemented by an agent program (concrete implementation). The \\\"vacuum-cleaner world\\\" is used as a simple example to illustrate these concepts.\\n\\n5. Good Behavior: The Concept of Rationality:\\nA rational agent performs actions that maximize a predefined performance measure (a criterion of success evaluating sequences of environment states). What is rational depends on:\\n   The performance measure.\\n   The agent\'s prior knowledge of the environment.\\n   The actions the agent can perform.\\n   The agent\'s percept sequence to date.\\nA rational agent should select actions that are expected to maximize its performance measure, given its percept sequence and built-in knowledge. An omniscient agent knows actual outcomes, but this is impossible; rationality maximizes expected performance. A rational agent should also be autonomous, learning from experience to compensate for partial or incorrect prior knowledge.\\n\\n6. Specifying the Task Environment (PEAS):\\nTask environments can be described by their PEAS (Performance, Environment, Actuators, Sensors) components. An automated taxi driver is used as a complex example:\\n   Performance: Correct destination, minimal fuel\\/wear, minimal trip time\\/cost, minimal traffic violations, maximal safety\\/comfort, maximal profits.\\n   Environment: Roads, traffic, pedestrians, animals, roadworks, weather, geographical variations.\\n   Actuators: Steering, accelerator, brakes, display screen\\/voice synthesizer, communication with other vehicles.\\n   Sensors: Video cameras, infrared\\/sonar, speedometer, accelerometer, engine\\/fuel sensors, GPS, keyboard\\/microphone for passenger input.\\n\\n7. Properties of Task Environments:\\nEnvironments are classified by properties that influence agent design:\\n   Fully Observable vs. Partially Observable: If sensors provide complete state information.\\n   Single Agent vs. Multiagent: If the agent operates alone or interacts with other agents (competitive or cooperative).\\n   Deterministic vs. Stochastic: If the next state is completely determined by the current state and action.\\n   Episodic vs. Sequential: If experiences are divided into atomic episodes or current decisions affect future ones.\\n   Static vs. Dynamic: If the environment changes while the agent is deliberating (semidynamic if only performance score changes).\\n   Discrete vs. Continuous: Applies to state, time, percepts, and actions.\\n   Known vs. Unknown: If outcomes of actions (or probabilities) are given.\\n\\n8. The Structure of Agents:\\nAI\'s goal is to design agent programs that implement the agent function. Four basic types of agent programs are introduced:\\n   Simple Reflex Agents: Select actions based only on the current percept, using condition-action rules. They are simple but limited, struggling with partially observable environments and prone to infinite loops. Randomization can help escape loops.\\n   Model-Based Reflex Agents: Handle partial observability by maintaining an internal state (a \\\"model of the world\\\") that tracks unobserved aspects. This requires knowledge of how the world evolves independently and how the agent\'s actions affect it.\\n   Goal-Based Agents: Combine the current state description with \\\"goal information\\\" (desirable situations) and a world model to choose actions that achieve goals, often requiring search and planning. They are more flexible than reflex agents as knowledge is explicit.\\n   Utility-Based Agents: When goals alone are insufficient for high-quality behavior, a utility function quantifies how \\\"happy\\\" different world states would make the agent. A rational utility-based agent chooses actions to maximize expected utility.\\n\\n9. Learning Agents:\\nA learning agent has four conceptual components:\\n   Learning Element: Responsible for making improvements to the performance element.\\n   Performance Element: Selects external actions.\\n   Critic: Provides feedback to the learning element on how well the agent is doing against a fixed performance standard.\\n   Problem Generator: Suggests exploratory actions to gather new, informative experiences.\\n\\n10. How the Components of Agent Programs Work (Representations):\\nAgent programs represent the environment in various ways:\\n   Atomic Representation: Each state is indivisible (e.g., city names in a driving route problem). Used in search, game-playing, Hidden Markov models, and Markov decision processes.\\n   Factored Representation: Each state is split into a fixed set of variables or attributes, allowing shared attributes between states (e.g., GPS location). Used in constraint satisfaction, propositional logic, planning, Bayesian networks, and machine learning.\\n   Structured Representation: Describes objects (e.g., cows, trucks) and their explicit relationships (e.g., \\\"cow is in front of truck\\\"). Underlies relational databases, first-order logic, first-order probability models, knowledge-based learning, and natural language understanding.\",\"sender\":\"bot\",\"model\":\"Summarizer\",\"attachment\":null},{\"text\":\"[Image attached: WhatsApp Image 2025-10-24 at 10.33.32 AM (1).jpeg] Please analyze this image.\",\"sender\":\"user\",\"model\":null,\"attachment\":{\"name\":\"WhatsApp Image 2025-10-24 at 10.33.32 AM (1).jpeg\",\"size\":228983,\"type\":\"image\\/jpeg\",\"url\":\"uploads\\/chat_images\\/img_1763139707_22231.jpeg\"}},{\"text\":\"API call failed: API Error: 503\",\"sender\":\"bot\",\"model\":\"Error\",\"attachment\":null},{\"text\":\"[Image attached: WhatsApp Image 2025-10-24 at 10.33.32 AM (1).jpeg] Please analyze this image.\",\"sender\":\"user\",\"model\":null,\"attachment\":{\"name\":\"WhatsApp Image 2025-10-24 at 10.33.32 AM (1).jpeg\",\"size\":228983,\"type\":\"image\\/jpeg\",\"url\":\"uploads\\/chat_images\\/img_1763139730_70892.jpeg\"}},{\"text\":\"API call failed: API Error: 503\",\"sender\":\"bot\",\"model\":\"Error\",\"attachment\":null},{\"text\":\"[File attached: notepad.txt] Please summarize this document.\",\"sender\":\"user\",\"model\":null,\"attachment\":{\"name\":\"notepad.txt\",\"size\":2219,\"type\":\"text\\/plain\",\"url\":null}},{\"text\":\"API call failed: API Error: 503\",\"sender\":\"bot\",\"model\":\"Error\",\"attachment\":null}]}', '2025-11-14 18:02:47', '2025-11-14 18:02:47', '2025-11-14 18:02:47'),

Thinking Humanly (Cognitive Modeling): Focuses on understanding how humans think through introspection, psychological experiments, and brain imaging, then replicating these thought processes in computer programs. Communication and randomized behavior can be rational in multiagent settings.\\n   Deterministic vs. stochastic: A deterministic environment\'s next state is completely determined by the current state and action. Examples include the Internet. **Switched WANs** are fundamental for global communication.\\n*   **Internetwork:** Formed when two or more networks are connected.\\n*   **Heterogeneous Network:** Connects diverse types of devices and network architectures.\\n*   **Switching:** The process of forwarding data packets.\\n    *   **Circuit Switching:** Establishes a fixed connection (efficient at full capacity, inefficient otherwise).\\n    *   **Packet Switching:** Data divided into packets (efficient, but can introduce delays with heavy traffic).\\n    *   **Message Switching:** Entire messages are stored and forwarded (obsolete).\\n*   **The Internet:** A global system of interconnected networks using **TCP\\/IP**.\\n*   **Accessing the Internet:** Methods include Dial-up, DSL, Cable, Fiber Optic, Satellite, Mobile Broadband, and Wi-Fi.\\n\\n#### 4. Routing algorithm for a node**, as indicated by \\\"Table 20.3 Path-vector algorithm for a node\\\".\\n\\n### Algorithm Overview:\\n\\nThe algorithm, named `Path_Vector_Routing()`, outlines the process a single node undertakes to manage and update its routing information. It\'s divided into two main phases: **Initialization** and **Update**.\\n\\n### Initialization Phase (Lines 4-12):\\n\\n1.  **Loop through Destinations:** The node iterates through all possible destinations, represented by `y` from 1 to `N`.\\n2.  **Determine Initial Path:**\\n    *   If `y` is the node itself (`y is myself`), the path to `y` is set to the node itself (`Path[y] = myself`).\\n    *   If `y` is a direct neighbor, the path is recorded as the node itself followed by the neighbor node (`Path[y] = myself + neighbor node`).\\n    *   For all other destinations not directly reachable or the node itself, the path is initially set to empty (`Path[y] = empty`).\\n3.  **Broadcast Initial Vector:** After initialization, the node sends its complete path vector `{Path[1], Path[2], ..., Path[y]}` to all its neighbors.\\n\\n### Update Phase (Lines 14-27):\\n\\n1.  **Continuous Operation:** This phase runs indefinitely (`repeat (forever)`).\\n2.  **Receive Neighbor Information:** The node waits to receive a path vector `Path_w` from a neighbor `w`.\\n3.  **Process Received Vector:** For each destination `y` in the received vector:\\n    *   **Loop Avoidance:** If `Path_w` already includes the current node (`Path_w includes myself`), this path is discarded to prevent routing loops.\\n    *   **Path Selection:** Otherwise, the node compares its current path to `y` (`Path[y]`) with the path proposed by the neighbor (`myself + Path_w[y]`, which means the path from the neighbor `w` to destination `y`, prepended with the current node). The algorithm selects the \\\"best\\\" path, presumably the shortest or most optimal one, and updates `Path[y]` accordingly.\\n4.  **Broadcast Changes:** If any change occurs in the node\'s path vector as a result of the update, the node sends the updated vector `{Path[1], Path[2], ..., Path[y]}` to all its neighbors.\\n\\n### Purpose:\\n\\nThe **Path-Vector Routing algorithm** aims to establish and maintain routing information by exchanging path vectors with neighbors. It includes mechanisms for initialization and continuous updates, with a critical step to avoid routing loops by checking for the presence of the current node in received paths.\",\"sender\":\"bot\",\"model\":\"Summarizer\",\"attachment\":null,\"suggestions\":[{\"text\":\"Explain path-vector routing algorithms in more detail.\",\"action\":\"Explain path-vector routing algorithms in more detail.\"},{\"text\":\"Compare path-vector routing with distance-vector routing.\",\"action\":\"Compare path-vector routing with distance-vector routing.\"},{\"text\":\"List common \'best\' path selection criteria in routing algorithms.\",\"action\":\"List common \'best\' path selection criteria in routing algorithms.\"}]},{\"text\":\"[File attached: BCS515B-module-1-pdf.pdf] Please summarize this document.\\ni am tensed. csn you summarize this for me?\",\"sender\":\"user\",\"model\":null,\"attachment\":{\"name\":\"BCS515B-module-1-pdf.pdf\",\"size\":1550912,\"type\":\"application\\/pdf\",\"url\":null}},{\"text\":\"I understand you\'re feeling tense, and I\'m here to help by summarizing the document for you.\\n\\n### Artificial Intelligence - BCS515B: Module 1 Summary\\n\\nThis module introduces **Artificial Intelligence (AI)**, defining it as a branch of computer science focused on creating **intelligent machines** that mimic human capabilities. These systems can learn and improve over time.\\n\\n#### Four Approaches to AI:\\n\\n1.  **Acting Humanly (Turing Test Approach):** Aims to create machines that can behave indistinguishably from humans. The Turing Test is a benchmark for this.\\n2.  **Thinking Humanly (Cognitive Modeling Approach):** Focuses on understanding human thought processes and replicating them in machines, often using insights from cognitive science.\\n3.  **Thinking Rationally (Laws of Thought Approach):** Based on formal logic and irrefutable reasoning, aiming to create systems that think logically.\\n4.  **Acting Rationally (Rational Agent Approach):** Emphasizes designing **rational agents** that act to achieve the best possible outcome or the best expected outcome, given their knowledge and the environment.\\n\\n#### Rational Agents:\\n\\n*   An **agent** perceives its environment through **sensors** and acts upon it using **actuators**.\\n*   A **rational agent** maximizes its performance measure by making the best decision based on its percept sequence and prior knowledge.\\n*   **Autonomy** is crucial, meaning agents should learn and adapt rather than relying solely on pre-programmed knowledge.\\n\\n#### Task Environments (PEAS Framework):\\n\\nEnvironments are characterized by:\\n*   **P**erformance Measure: How success is evaluated.\\n*   **E**nvironment: The external world the \\\"Artificial Intelligence - BCS515B Module 1\\\"\\n\\nThis document introduces the fundamental concepts of **Artificial Intelligence (AI)**, defining it as a branch of computer science focused on creating **intelligent machines** that mimic human capabilities.\\n\\n#### Key Concepts:\\n\\n*   **Definition of AI:** AI systems are machines that simulate human intelligence to perform tasks and improve over time based on collected data.\\n*   **Scope of AI:** AI is a universal field encompassing diverse subfields, from general learning and perception to specific tasks like game playing, theorem proving, and medical diagnosis.\\n\\n#### Four Approaches to AI:\\n\\n1.  **Acting Humanly (Turing Test):** This approach focuses on a machine\'s ability to exhibit behavior indistinguishable from a human\'s, as proposed by Alan Turing. It requires capabilities like computer vision and robotics.\\n2.  **Thinking Humanly (Cognitive Modeling):** This approach seeks to understand how humans think and then build computer programs that mirror these cognitive processes. It involves introspection, psychological experiments, and brain imaging.\\n3.  **Thinking Rationally (\\\"Laws of Thought\\\"):** Based on the principles of logic, this approach aims to create systems that reason irrefutably. It faces challenges in formalizing informal knowledge and bridging theoretical problem-solving with practical application.\\n4.  **Acting Rationally (Rational Agent Approach):** This approach defines an agent as an entity that perceives its environment and acts upon it. A rational agent aims to achieve the best possible outcome, or the best expected outcome, given its knowledge. This approach is considered more general and amenable to scientific development.\\n\\n#### State of the Art in AI:\\n\\nThe document highlights various real-world AI applications, including:\\n\\n*   **Robotic Vehicles:** Self-driving cars like STANLEY and BOSS.\\n*   **Speech Recognition:** Automated systems for customer service.\\n*   **Autonomous Planning and Scheduling:** NASA\'s programs for spacecraft operations (Remote Agent, MAPGEN).\\n*   **Game Playing:** IBM\'s DEEP BLUE defeating a chess champion.\\n*   **Spam Fighting:** Learning algorithms that classify billions of emails daily.\\n*   **Logistics Planning:** Systems like DART used by U.S. forces.\\n*   **Robotics:** Consumer robots like Roomba and industrial robots like PackBot.\\n*   **Machine Translation:** Statistical models for translating languages.\\n\\n#### Agents and Environments:\\n\\n*   **Agent:** An entity that perceives its environment through sensors and acts through actuators.\\n*   **Percept:** The agent\'s perceptual input at a given moment.\\n*   **Percept Sequence:** The complete history of an agent\'s perceptions.\\n*   **Agent Function:** A mathematical description mapping percept sequences to actions.\\n*   **Agent Program:** A concrete implementation of the agent function.\\n\\n#### Rationality and Performance Measure:\\n\\n*   A **rational agent** selects actions that are expected to maximize its performance measure, considering its prior knowledge and current percepts.\\n*   The **performance measure** evaluates the desirability of environment states.\\n*   Key aspects influencing rationality include the performance measure, prior knowledge, available actions, and percept sequence.\\n*   **Omniscience** (knowing actual outcomes) is impossible; The `best` function compares the current `Path[y]` with a potential new path formed by prepending \\\"myself\\\" to the received path from the neighbor (`myself + Path_w[y]`). The shorter or more preferred path is chosen.\\n3.  **Vector Update and Broadcast:** If any change occurs in the node\'s path vector after processing the incoming vector, the updated vector `{Path[1], Path[2], ..., Path[y]}` is sent to all neighbors.\\n\\nThis algorithm is designed to allow nodes to discover and maintain routing paths to other nodes in a network, dynamically updating them as network conditions change and preventing routing loops.\",\"sender\":\"bot\",\"model\":\"Summarizer\",\"attachment\":null,\"suggestions\":[]},{\"text\":\"[File attached: BCS501-module-1-pdf.pdf] Please summarize this document.\\ni am tensed. can you summarize this for me?\",\"sender\":\"user\",\"model\":null,\"attachment\":{\"name\":\"BCS501-module-1-pdf.pdf\",\"size\":979478,\"type\":\"application\\/pdf\",\"url\":null}},{\"text\":\"It\'s completely understandable to feel tense when you\'re facing new material. Errors are in design or code, not physical degradation.\\n        *   **Doesn\'t \\\"Wear Out\\\":** Hardware fails due to physical aging, whereas software failures indicate design or coding errors. Software *deteriorates* due to frequent changes.\\n        *   **Custom-built:** Often developed uniquely rather than assembled from standard components.\\n        *   **Reusable components are desired:** The industry aims for reusable libraries (e.g., GUI elements).\\n\\n*   **Software Application Domains:**\\n    *   **System Software:** Supports other programs (e.g., operating systems, compilers).\\n    *   **Application Software:** Solves specific business needs (e.g., point-of-sale systems).\\n    *   **Engineering\\/Scientific Software:** Handles complex computations (\\\"number crunching\\\").\\n    *   **Embedded Software:** Resides within products to control features (e.g., car systems).\\n    *   **Product-line Software:** Designed for multiple customers (e.g., inventory control).\\n    *   **Web Applications:** Client-server programs running in browsers.\\n    *   **Artificial Intelligence Software:** Uses non-numerical algorithms (e.g., expert systems, pattern recognition).\\n\\n*   **New Software Challenges:**\\n    *   **Open-world computing:** Interconnectivity across devices.\\n    *   **Net sourcing:** Developing applications for global markets via the web.\\n    *   **Open Source:** Distributing code for modification and reuse.\\n\\n*   **Legacy Software:**\\n    *   Older programs often have poor quality (inextensible design, convoluted code).\\n time-to-market), security concerns, and aesthetics**.\\n\\n*   **Software Engineering as a Layered Technology:**\\n    *   It rests on a **quality focus** (bedrock).\\n    *   The **process layer** provides a framework for development.\\n    *   **Methods** offer technical guidance for tasks (communication, analysis, design, coding, testing).\\n    *   **Tools** automate or semi-automate methods (CASE tools).\\n\\n*   **The Software Process:**\\n    *   A collection of **activities, actions, and tasks**.\\n    *   A **process framework** defines foundation activities (Communication, Planning, Modeling, Construction, Deployment) and **umbrella activities** (tracking, risk management, quality assurance, reviews, measurement, configuration management, reusability, work product preparation).\\n    *   Processes should be **agile and adaptable**.\\n\\n*   **The Software Engineering Practice:**\\n    *   **Essence:** Understand the problem, plan a solution, carry out the plan, examine the result.\\n    *   **General Principles:** Provide value, keep it simple (KISS), maintain vision, be considerate of consumers, be open to the future, plan for reuse, and think before acting.\\n\\n*   **Software Myths:**\\n    *   False beliefs about software development that can mislead managers and customers. Examples include humans, robots, and software.\\n*   **Percepts and Percept Sequence:** A percept is the agent\'s sensory input at a given moment, and a percept sequence is the history of all perceptions. An agent\'s action can depend on its entire percept sequence.\\n*   **Agent Function vs. Agent Program:** The agent function is an abstract mapping from percept sequences to actions, while the agent program is the concrete implementation running on a physical system.\\n*   **Rationality:** A rational agent maximizes its performance measure. --
-- Table structure for table `feedback`

CREATE TABLE `feedback` (
  `id` int(11) NOT NULL,
  `user_id` int(11) DEFAULT NULL,
  `user_name` varchar(255) DEFAULT NULL,
  `user_email` varchar(255) DEFAULT NULL,
  `message` text NOT NULL,
  `timestamp` timestamp NOT NULL DEFAULT current_timestamp()
) ENGINE=InnoDB DEFAULT CHARSET=utf8mb4 COLLATE=utf8mb4_general_ci;

-- Table structure for table `reminders`

  `title` varchar(255) NOT NULL,

  `created_at` datetime DEFAULT current_timestamp()
) ENGINE=InnoDB DEFAULT CHARSET=utf8mb4 COLLATE=utf8mb4_general_ci;

-- Table structure for table `users`
